The Second Premise: Everything Possible Is Originated
Imam Razi proves the second premise of the fourth proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why everything possible in itself must be originated, and thus everything other than God is originated.

Core Idea
The possible needs a cause to tip the balance from non-existence to existence, making it originated.

Having established that everything other than God is possible, Imam Razi now proves that everything possible is originated. The argument relies on the nature of the possible and the impossibility of a cause acting on an already existing thing. This lesson unpacks that proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two sub-premises
The passage has two sub-arguments: first, the possible needs an effecting cause; second, that cause must act at origination, not during continuance.
2
Understand why the possible needs an effecting cause
The possible is neutral between existence and non-existence, so an external cause is needed to prefer existence.
This is the principle of determination (tarjīḥ).
3
See why dependence on the cause cannot occur during continuance
If the possible needed a cause during its continued existence, that would require re-creating what already exists, which is absurd. So the need must be at the moment of origination or in non-existence.
Thus the possible is originated (muḥdath).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الرابع في حدوث ما سوی الله تعالى : فنقول : كل ما سوى الواجب الوجود الواحد فإنه ممكن لذاته، وكل ممكن لذاته فهو محدث، فإذن كل ما سوى الموجود الواحد فإنه محدث. بيان المقدمة الأولى وهي قولنا : كل ما سوى الموجود الواحد فهو ممكن لذاته، فنقول : الدليل عليه أنا لو فرضنا موجودين يكون كل واحد منهما واجبًا لذاته فلا بد وأن يكونا متشاركين في الوجوب الذاتي، ولا بد وأن يكونا غير متشاركين في التعيين، وما به الاشتراك غير ما به الامتياز، فإذن يكون كل واحد منهما مركبا من الوجود الذاتي الذي حصلت به المشاركة ومن التعيين الذي به حصلت المباينة لكن كل مركب فإنه مفتقر في ماهيته وفي تحققه إلى كل واحد من مفرديه، وكل واحد من مفرديه مغاير له ؛ لأن الكل مغاير لكل واحد من أجزائه، فإذن كل مركب فإنه مفتقر في تحققه إلى غيره وكل مفتقر في تحققه إلى غيره فهو ممكن لذاته، فإذن كل مركب فهو ممكن لذاته فإذن لو فرضنا موجودين واجبي الوجود لكان كل واحد منهما ممكنا لذاته والثاني محال فإذن فرض موجودين واجبي الوجود يجب أن يكون محالاً، فثبت أن كل ما سوى الموجود الواحد يجب أن يكون ممكنا لذاته. وأما المقدمة الثانية وهي أن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فإنه يجب أن يكون محدثاً، فالبرهان على صحته أن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فإنه مفتقر في رجحان وجوده على عدمه إلى المؤثر، وكل ما كان مفتقرًا في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإنه يجب أن يكون محدثًا. بيان المقدمة الأولى: أن الممكن ما تكون ماهيته قابلة للعدم والوجود على البدل، وما كان كذلك امتنع رجحان أحد الطرفين على الآخر إلا لمؤثر منفصل. بيان المقدمة الثانية : أن نقول : الافتقار إلى المؤثر إما أن يحصل حال الوجود أو حال العدم، فإن حصل حال الوجود فإما أن يحصل حال البقاء أو محال الحدوث، ولا جائز أن يحصل حال البقاء، وإلا لزم أن يكون الشيء حال بقائه مفتقرًا إلى موجد يوجده ، وإلى مكون يكونه، وذلك محال ؛ لأن إيجاد الموجود تحصيل حاصل، وتحصيل الحاصل محال في بداهة العقول فلم يبق إلا أن يكون افتقار الأثر إلى المؤثر إما حاصلا حال الحدوث أو حال العدم، وعلى التقديرين فإنه يلزم أن يكون كل مفتقر في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإنه يكون محدثاً، فثبت أن كل ما سوى الواحد ممكن لذاته وثبت أن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فهو مفتقر في وجوده إلى المؤثر، وثبت أن كل ما كان مفتقرًا في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإذن يلزم من هذا البرهان أن كل ما سوى الواحد لا بد وأن يكون محدثًا . وهذا البرهان يفيد حدوث الأجسام والأعراض، والعقول والنفوس والهيولى، ويفيد أن واجب الوجود واحد وهو جل جلاله وبالجملة فهو برهان عظيم وافٍ بإثبات أكثر المباحث الشريفة الإلهية.
The fourth proof concerning the origination of what is other than God, the Exalted: We say: Everything other than the One Necessary Existent is possible in itself, and everything possible in itself is originated. Therefore, everything other than the One Existent is originated. Explanation of the first premise, which is our statement: 'Everything other than the One Existent is possible in itself.' We say: The proof for it is that if we suppose two existents each necessary in themselves, they must share in essential necessity and must differ in individuation. That by which they share is other than that by which they differ. Thus each would be composed of the essential existence by which sharing occurs and the individuation by which distinction occurs. But every composite is dependent in its quiddity and realization on each of its parts, and each of its parts is other than it because the whole is other than each of its parts. Therefore every composite is dependent in its realization on something other than itself, and everything dependent in its realization on something other than itself is possible in itself. Thus every composite is possible in itself. Therefore, if we suppose two existents necessary in themselves, each would be possible in itself, which is impossible. Hence the supposition of two necessary existents must be impossible. Thus it is established that everything other than the One Existent must be possible in itself. As for the second premise, that everything possible in itself must be originated: the proof of its correctness is that everything possible in itself is dependent for the preponderance of its existence over its non-existence on an effecting cause, and everything dependent in its existence on an effecting cause must be originated. Explanation of the first [sub-]premise: The possible is that whose quiddity is receptive of non-existence and existence alternately, and when that is so, the preponderance of one side over the other is impossible except through a separate effecting cause. Explanation of the second [sub-]premise: We say: Dependence on the effecting cause occurs either in the state of existence or in the state of non-existence. If it occurs in the state of existence, then either in the state of continuance or at the moment of origination. It cannot occur in the state of continuance, otherwise it would require that a thing in its state of continuance be dependent on an originator to originate it and a maker to make it, which is impossible because bringing the existent into existence is a reactualization of what already exists, and reactualization of what already exists is impossible in the immediate judgment of intellects. Thus nothing remains except that the dependence of the effect on the effecting cause occurs either at the moment of origination or in the state of non-existence. On either assumption, it follows that everything dependent in its existence on an effecting cause is originated. So it is established that everything other than the One is possible in itself, and it is established that everything possible in itself is dependent in its existence on an effecting cause, and it is established that everything dependent in its existence on an effecting cause is originated. Therefore it follows from this proof that everything other than the One must be originated. And this proof yields the origination of bodies, accidents, intellects, souls, and prime matter, and it yields that the Necessary Existent is One – He is majestic is His glory – and in summary it is a great proof sufficient for establishing most of the noble divine investigations.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained proof (burhān) for the existence of the One Necessary Existent and the origination of all else. It proceeds in two premises. First premise: Everything other than the One is possible in itself. The author demonstrates this by showing that if there were two necessary existents, they would share necessity and differ in individuality, making each composite. Since composition entails dependence and dependence entails possibility, both would be possible, contradicting necessity. Therefore only one necessary existent can exist, and everything else is possible. Second premise: Everything possible is originated (muḥdath). The argumentation here is twofold. The possible, by definition, is equally receptive to existence and non-existence, so it needs an external cause (muʼaththir) to tip the balance. This dependence must occur either at the moment of origination or in the state of non-existence (since dependence during continuance is impossible – that would be re-creating what already exists, which is absurd). Thus the possible is originated. The conclusion: everything other than the One is originated. The author then notes the wide scope of this proof: it applies to bodies, accidents, intellects, souls, and prime matter, establishing both the unity of God and the origination of the world.

Key Terms
ممكن لذاته (possible in itself)
مؤثر (effecting cause)
محدث (originated)
ترجيح (preponderance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'possible' means 'maybe exists and maybe not', but here it specifically means dependent on a cause for existence.
Correction: The possible is defined as equally receptive to existence and non-existence, requiring an external cause to become actual.

Checkpoint
Why cannot a possible thing depend on an effecting cause during its state of continuance?
A) Because continuance is permanent.
B) Because that would require re-creating what already exists, which is impossible.
C) Because the cause only acts in the past.
D) Because continuance does not need a cause.

Key Takeaway
Everything possible in itself requires a cause to bring it into existence, and that cause acts at the moment of origination, making the possible originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a possible being – your existence is not necessary. Do you live as if you could have never existed? What would change today if you truly internalized that every breath is a gift that could have been withheld?
?
The proof shows that your dependence on Allah is at the moment of your creation, not in your continuance. Does this lead you to think you are self-sufficient now? How does this relate to your need for Allah for guidance, provision, and every good?
?
Imam al-Razi says this proof yields that everything other than Allah is originated. Is there any created thing you love or fear as if it were eternal? What would it look like to uproot that from your heart?

Objection and First Answer on Shared Negatives
Objection to the fourth proof and the first answer regarding negative attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how an objector challenges the fourth proof by denying that other-than-One is possible, and the author's first answer that a shared negative attribute does not cause composition.

Core Idea
A shared negative attribute does not entail composition in quiddity.

This passage presents a critical objection to the fourth proof for divine oneness. The objector denies the premise that everything other than the One is possible, and then argues that if two necessary existents were supposed, they would be composite—contradicting necessity. The author responds with the first of several answers, showing that sharing a negative attribute does not necessitate composition, using the analogy of two simple quiddities.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Notice the objector's denial of the premise 'what is other than the One is possible' and the restatement of the proof's reasoning leading to composition.
The objector uses the proof's own logic against it.
2
Identify the author's first answer
Focus on the claim that necessity of existence is a negative attribute, and that sharing a negative attribute does not cause composition in quiddity.
The author gives a reductio: if sharing negatives caused composition, then every simple would be composite.
3
Reflect on the logical structure
Understand how the author defends against the composition objection by distinguishing between sharing negative and positive attributes.
This answer is the first of several, indicating the depth of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا نسلم أن ما سوى الواحد ممكن لذاته . قوله: "لو فرضنا موجودين يكون كل واحد منهما واجباً لذاته لكانا متشاركين في الوجوب الذاتي ومتباينين في التعين فحينئذ يكون كل واحد منهما مركباً، وكل مركب ممكن، فحينئذ يكون الواجب لذاته ممكناً لذاته ". قلنا : لا نسلم أنه يلزم من فرض كون كل واحد منهما واجبًا لذاته وقوع التركيب وبيانه من وجوه أحدها: أن بتقدير أن يكون وجوب الوجود وصفًا سلبياً، يكون كل واحد منهما مشاركًا للآخر في وصف سلبي، ويكون كل واحد منهما مباينا للآخر في تمام الماهية. فالاشتراك في وصف السلبي لا يوجب وقوع التركيب في الماهية؛ بدليل أن كل ماهيتين بسيطتين، فلا بد وأن يشتركا في سلب ما عداهما عنهما، فلو كان الاشتراك في السلوب يوجب وقوع الكثرة في الماهية لزم أن يكون كل بسيط مركبا
If it is said: 'We do not accept that what is other than the One is possible in itself. His statement: 'If we suppose two existents each necessary in themselves, they would share in essential necessity and differ in individuation; thus each would be composite, and every composite is possible; thus the necessary in itself would be possible in itself.' We say: We do not accept that from the supposition of each being necessary in itself composition necessarily follows. Its explanation [is given] in several ways. One of them: That on the assumption that necessity of existence is a negative attribute, each would share with the other in a negative attribute, and each would be distinct from the other in the entire quiddity. Thus sharing in a negative attribute does not cause composition in the quiddity; as evidenced by the fact that every two simple quiddities must share in the negation of what is other than them from themselves. If sharing in negations caused multiplicity in the quiddity, then every simple would be composite.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an objection (iʽtirāḍ) and the author's first answer (jawāb). The objector attacks the first premise of the fourth proof, denying that everything other than the One is possible. The objector restates the argument: if there were two necessary existents, they would share in essential necessity and differ in individuation, leading to composition and hence possibility. But the objector counters that if necessity of existence is a negative attribute (waṣf salbī), then sharing a negation does not entail composition. He gives an example: two simple quiddities both share the negation of everything else, yet they remain simple. If shared negations caused composition, then every simple would be composite – a contradiction. Therefore, the objector argues, the original reasoning fails. The author here presents this objection and begins his reply, stating that he does not accept that composition follows, and he will provide several explanations. The first explanation is given in full: even if necessity is a negative attribute, the shared negative still creates a distinction between the shared aspect and the specific quiddity, leading to composition. But the text ends mid-argument, noting that if shared negatives caused composition, then every simple would be composite – which is the objector's point. The author presumably continues with further answers on the next page.

Key Terms

ماهية
بسيط
تركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection successfully refutes the fourth proof.
Correction: The author provides an answer that counters the objection by showing that a shared negative attribute does not entail composition, thus the objection is not conclusive.

Checkpoint
What is the objector's main attempt to avoid composition?
A) Claiming the two existents are identical.
B) Claiming necessity is a positive attribute that unifies.
C) Claiming necessity is a negative attribute, so sharing it does not cause composition.
D) Claiming composition does not imply possibility.

Key Takeaway
The author's first answer to the objection is that a shared negative attribute does not cause composition in quiddity, as shown by simple quiddities sharing negations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that sharing a negative attribute does not cause composition. Now examine your own understanding of tawheed: do you ever inadvertently imagine Allah's attributes as separate 'parts' added to His essence? How does this answer about negative attributes correct that? What will you do to ensure your belief in Allah's oneness remains pure from any notion of composition?
?
The objector assumed that any common attribute between two entities forces a multiplicity in their essences. In your life, when you share a negative quality (like lack of patience) with someone else, do you feel that it compromises your individuality? How does this lesson's emphasis on the simplicity of quiddities challenge you to see that your distinctness is not threatened by shared negations? What does this teach you about Allah's utter uniqueness despite His attributes being shared in name?
?
The author uses the example of two simple quiddities that both lack everything other than themselves. Reflect on your own self-definition: how much of your identity is built on what you are not (negations) rather than what you are? Does this remind you that Allah's descriptions of Himself are not like human descriptions? Commit to studying His names and attributes with the understanding that they are not composite.

The First Premise: Definition of the Possible and Its Need for a Cause
Razi defines the possible and states its need for a cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a possible being (mumkin) and why it requires an external efficient cause to bring it into existence.

Core Idea
A possible being is equally open to existence and non-existence, so it needs a cause to tip the scale.

The proof of God’s existence often begins with the observation that the world is contingent. Razi starts by defining what it means for something to be possible (mumkin) — a being whose essence is not inherently existent or non-existent. This definition is the first building block of the proof that everything besides God requires a cause and is therefore originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Note the structure: a general statement, then an explanation of the first premise.
The passage begins with the conclusion that whatever depends on a cause is originated, then explains the first premise.
2
Identify the definition of 'possible'
Find how Razi defines 'mumkin' (possible). Notice that it is defined by its essence being receptive to both existence and non-existence, without inherent preponderance.
This definition is crucial: it sets up the need for an external cause.
3
Understand why an external cause is necessary
The passage states that without a separate efficient cause, the two sides (existence and non-existence) cannot be preponderated. Grasp why a cause must be separate from the possible being itself.
If the cause were part of the essence, the being would be self-sufficient, contradicting possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الثالثة على عدمه إلى المؤثر، وكل ما كان مفتقرًا في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإنه يجب أن يكون محدثًا. بيان المقدمة الأولى: أن الممكن ما تكون ماهيته قابلة للعدم والوجود على البدل، وما كان كذلك امتنع رجحان أحد الطرفين على الآخر إلا لمؤثر منفصل. بيان المقدمة الثانية : أن نقول : الافتقار إلى المؤثر إما أن يحصل حال الوجود أو حال العدم، فإن حصل حال الوجود فإما أن يحصل حال البقاء أو محال الحدوث، ولا جائز أن يحصل حال البقاء، وإلا لزم أن يكون الشيء حال بقائه مفتقرًا إلى موجد يوجده ، وإلى مكون يكونه، وذلك محال ؛ لأن إيجاد الموجود تحصيل حاصل، وتحصيل الحاصل محال في بداهة العقول فلم يبق إلا أن يكون افتقار الأثر إلى المؤثر إما حاصلا حال الحدوث أو حال العدم، وعلى التقديرين فإنه يلزم أن يكون كل مفتقر في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإنه يكون محدثاً، فثبت أن كل ما سوى الواحد ممكن لذاته وثبت أن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فهو مفتقر في وجوده إلى المؤثر، وثبت أن كل ما كان مفتقرًا في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإذن يلزم من هذا البرهان أن كل ما سوى الواحد لا بد وأن يكون محدثًا . وهذا البرهان يفيد حدوث الأجسام والأعراض، والعقول والنفوس والهيولى، ويفيد أن واجب الوجود واحد وهو جل جلاله وبالجملة فهو برهان عظيم وافٍ بإثبات أكثر المباحث الشريفة الإلهية.
The third introduction: [Everything that is] dependent in its existence upon the efficient cause must be originated (muhdath). Explanation of the first premise: The possible (mumkin) is that whose essence is receptive of non-existence and existence alternately, and being such, the preponderance of one of the two sides over the other is impossible except by a separate efficient cause. Explanation of the second premise: We say: The need for the efficient cause either obtains in the state of existence or in the state of non-existence. If it obtains in the state of existence, then either it obtains in the state of continuance or in the state of origination. It is not possible that it obtains in the state of continuance, otherwise it would necessitate that something in its state of continuance needs a bringer into existence to bring it into existence and a maker to make it, which is impossible because bringing into existence what already exists is a reacquisition, and reacquisition of what is already acquired is impossible according to the primary dictates of the intellect. Thus it remains that the need of the effect for the efficient cause either obtains in the state of origination or in the state of non-existence. In both cases, it necessitates that everything that depends in its existence upon the efficient cause is originated. So it is established that everything other than the One is possible in itself, and it is established that everything that is possible in itself depends in its existence upon the efficient cause, and it is established that everything that depends in its existence upon the efficient cause is originated. Therefore, from this proof it follows that everything other than the One must be originated. This proof yields the origination of bodies, accidents, intellects, souls, and hyle, and it yields that the Necessary Existent is One, exalted is His majesty. In sum, it is a great proof sufficient for establishing most of the noble divine investigations.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a complete proof of the contingency (temporal origination) of everything other than God. The proof is structured as a third introduction (muqaddima) to the overall argument. It begins by stating the conclusion that everything dependent on an efficient cause (mu'aththir) is originated (muhdath). Then it explains the first premise: a possible being (mumkin) is one whose essence is equally receptive to existence and non-existence; such a being requires an external cause to tip the balance toward existence. The second premise examines the timing of this need for a cause. It cannot be during the state of continued existence, because that would entail reacquiring what is already possessed, which is absurd. Therefore the need must be either at the moment of origination or in the state of non-existence. In either case, the thing is originated (hadith). The proof concludes that all besides God are originated, and this proves the oneness of the Necessary Existent. The author notes that this proof covers bodies, accidents, intellects, souls, and prime matter, and is sufficient for most divine topics.

Key Terms
ممكن
مؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that possibility alone implies temporal origination without need for a cause.
Correction: Razi shows that possibility requires a cause to bring about existence, but the definition itself does not yet prove origination; it only establishes dependence. The proof of origination comes in the second premise.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is a possible being (mumkin)?
A) Something that cannot exist
B) Something whose essence is equally receptive to both existence and non-existence
C) Something that always exists
D) Something that does not need a cause

Key Takeaway
A possible being is one that requires an external efficient cause to bring it into existence because its essence is neutral toward existence and non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a possible being. Your essence could just as easily have been non-existent. Does your daily life reflect humble dependence on the One who tipped the scale for you, or do you live as though existence is your own right?
?
If your essence is neutral toward existence, what does that imply about your ultimate purpose? Who gave you being, and what claim does that give Him over your choices today?
?
How would your attitude toward trials change if you truly believed that every moment of your existence is sustained moment by moment by the efficient cause, not by your own power?

The Second Premise: The Timing of Need and the Conclusion
Razi argues for the timing of need for cause and concludes all else is originated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the need for an efficient cause must be at the point of origination or non-existence, and how this leads to the conclusion that everything other than God is originated.

Core Idea
A thing cannot need a cause while it already exists; it must need it before existence or at origination, proving it is originated.

After establishing that possible beings need a cause, Razi examines exactly when that need occurs. He argues compellingly that the need cannot be during the state of continuance (baga'), because that would mean trying to acquire what is already possessed. This leads to the conclusion that everything contingent is temporally originated (muhdath), and only the Necessary Existent is unoriginated.

Guided Path
1
Read the second premise passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the logical division: the need for a cause can be either in the state of existence or non-existence. Then within existence, it is either during continuance or origination.
Identify the three possibilities: during continuance, during origination, or during non-existence.
2
Understand the rejection of continuance
The passage argues that needing a cause during continuance would entail 'reacquiring what is already acquired' (tahsil al-hasil), which is rationally absurd. Grasp why this is impossible.
This is a key move: if the thing already exists, it cannot need a cause to exist again.
3
Follow the remaining possibilities and conclusion
After eliminating continuance, the need must be either at origination or non-existence. In both cases, the thing is originated (hadith), because it either comes into existence at a time or is preceded by non-existence.
The conclusion: everything besides the One is originated.
4
Appreciate the scope of the proof
Razi notes that this proof covers not only bodies and accidents but also intellects, souls, and prime matter—everything except God.
This shows the comprehensiveness of the argument.

المقدمة الثالثة على عدمه إلى المؤثر، وكل ما كان مفتقرًا في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإنه يجب أن يكون محدثًا. بيان المقدمة الأولى: أن الممكن ما تكون ماهيته قابلة للعدم والوجود على البدل، وما كان كذلك امتنع رجحان أحد الطرفين على الآخر إلا لمؤثر منفصل. بيان المقدمة الثانية : أن نقول : الافتقار إلى المؤثر إما أن يحصل حال الوجود أو حال العدم، فإن حصل حال الوجود فإما أن يحصل حال البقاء أو محال الحدوث، ولا جائز أن يحصل حال البقاء، وإلا لزم أن يكون الشيء حال بقائه مفتقرًا إلى موجد يوجده ، وإلى مكون يكونه، وذلك محال ؛ لأن إيجاد الموجود تحصيل حاصل، وتحصيل الحاصل محال في بداهة العقول فلم يبق إلا أن يكون افتقار الأثر إلى المؤثر إما حاصلا حال الحدوث أو حال العدم، وعلى التقديرين فإنه يلزم أن يكون كل مفتقر في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإنه يكون محدثاً، فثبت أن كل ما سوى الواحد ممكن لذاته وثبت أن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فهو مفتقر في وجوده إلى المؤثر، وثبت أن كل ما كان مفتقرًا في وجوده إلى المؤثر فإذن يلزم من هذا البرهان أن كل ما سوى الواحد لا بد وأن يكون محدثًا . وهذا البرهان يفيد حدوث الأجسام والأعراض، والعقول والنفوس والهيولى، ويفيد أن واجب الوجود واحد وهو جل جلاله وبالجملة فهو برهان عظيم وافٍ بإثبات أكثر المباحث الشريفة الإلهية.
The third introduction: [Everything that is] dependent in its existence upon the efficient cause must be originated (muhdath). Explanation of the first premise: The possible (mumkin) is that whose essence is receptive of non-existence and existence alternately, and being such, the preponderance of one of the two sides over the other is impossible except by a separate efficient cause. Explanation of the second premise: We say: The need for the efficient cause either obtains in the state of existence or in the state of non-existence. If it obtains in the state of existence, then either it obtains in the state of continuance or in the state of origination. It is not possible that it obtains in the state of continuance, otherwise it would necessitate that something in its state of continuance needs a bringer into existence to bring it into existence and a maker to make it, which is impossible because bringing into existence what already exists is a reacquisition, and reacquisition of what is already acquired is impossible according to the primary dictates of the intellect. Thus it remains that the need of the effect for the efficient cause either obtains in the state of origination or in the state of non-existence. In both cases, it necessitates that everything that depends in its existence upon the efficient cause is originated. So it is established that everything other than the One is possible in itself, and it is established that everything that is possible in itself depends in its existence upon the efficient cause, and it is established that everything that depends in its existence upon the efficient cause is originated. Therefore, from this proof it follows that everything other than the One must be originated. This proof yields the origination of bodies, accidents, intellects, souls, and hyle, and it yields that the Necessary Existent is One, exalted is His majesty. In sum, it is a great proof sufficient for establishing most of the noble divine investigations.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a complete proof of the contingency (temporal origination) of everything other than God. The proof is structured as a third introduction (muqaddima) to the overall argument. It begins by stating the conclusion that everything dependent on an efficient cause (mu'aththir) is originated (muhdath). Then it explains the first premise: a possible being (mumkin) is one whose essence is equally receptive to existence and non-existence; such a being requires an external cause to tip the balance toward existence. The second premise examines the timing of this need for a cause. It cannot be during the state of continued existence, because that would entail reacquiring what is already possessed, which is absurd. Therefore the need must be either at the moment of origination or in the state of non-existence. In either case, the thing is originated (hadith). The proof concludes that all besides God are originated, and this proves the oneness of the Necessary Existent. The author notes that this proof covers bodies, accidents, intellects, souls, and prime matter, and is sufficient for most divine topics.

مؤثر
محدث
واجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if something needs a cause during its existence, it can still be eternal.
Correction: Razi shows that needing a cause during continuance is absurd; thus the need must be at the beginning or before existence, proving temporal origination.

Checkpoint
Why can the need for an efficient cause not be during the state of continuance?
A) Because it would lead to an infinite regress
B) Because it would involve reacquiring what already exists, which is impossible
C) Because continuance is the same as origination
D) Because the cause would then be unnecessary

Key Takeaway
The need for a cause cannot be during continuance, so it must be at origination or non-existence, proving that all that depends on a cause is temporally originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything besides Allah is originated and dependent on Him for its existence, what does that mean for your attachment to any created thing—your health, wealth, relationships, or even your own life? Are you investing your heart in something that is itself constantly in need? How can you shift your ultimate trust to the Self-Sufficient alone starting today?
?
Razi proves that the need for a cause cannot be during continuance: a thing does not need a cause after it exists. But do you act as though you need Allah only for your initial existence, or do you recognize your continuous dependence on Him for every breath and every moment of existence? What would change in your daily awareness if you truly believed that your very continuance is a new creation each instant?
?
The proof concludes that the Necessary Existent is One. Examine your life: where have you ascribed independence or ultimate causality to something other than Allah—perhaps in relying on your own strength, intellect, or the support of others as if they were self-sufficient? Commit to one concrete way today to affirm that He alone is the true Cause.

Objection and Reply: Two Necessary Beings
Razi presents and replies to an objection against multiple necessary beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the objection that two necessary beings would be composite.

Core Idea
Sharing a negative attribute does not make a simple thing composite.

This lesson presents a classic objection against the possibility of multiple necessary beings: that they would be composite and hence contingent. Razi replies by showing that if necessity is a negative attribute, sharing it does not entail composition. We will examine the objection and the first part of his reply.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Identify the structure: the objector assumes two necessary beings, notes they share necessity and differ in specificity, concludes each is composite, and hence possible, contradicting necessity.
2
Understand the reply's core argument
Razi denies that composition follows. He posits that if necessity is a negative attribute, then sharing a negative attribute does not cause composition. Note his example of two simple essences sharing negations.
This is one of several aspects Razi mentions.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this argument matters for tawhid: it defends the unity of God by showing that multiplicity of necessary beings is not logically forced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا نسلم أن ما سوى الواحد ممكن لذاته . قوله: "لو فرضنا موجودين يكون كل واحد منهما واجباً لذاته لكانا متشاركين في الوجوب الذاتي ومتباينين في التعين فحينئذ يكون كل واحد منهما مركباً، وكل مركب ممكن، فحينئذ يكون الواجب لذاته ممكنا لذاته ". قلنا : لا نسلم أنه يلزم من فرض كون كل واحد منهما واجبًا لذاته وقوع التركيب وبيانه من وجوه أحدها: أن بتقدير أن يكون وجوب الوجود وصفًا سلبياً، يكون كل واحد منهما مشاركًا للآخر في وصف سلبي، ويكون كل واحد منهما مباينا للآخر في تمام الماهية. فالاشتراك في وصف السلبي لا يوجب وقوع التركيب في الماهية؛ بدليل أن كل ماهيتين بسيطتين، فلا بد وأن يشتركا في سلب ما عداهما عنهما، فلو كان الاشتراك في السلوب يوجب وقوع الكثرة في الماهية لزم أن يكون كل بسيط مركبا وذلك محال، فعلمنا أن بتقدير أن يكون وجوب الوجود وصفا لا يلزم وقوع الكثرة.
It might be said: We do not accept that everything other than the One is possible in itself. Its statement: "If we suppose two existents each of which is necessary in itself, they would share in essential necessity and differ in specificity; then each of them would be composite, and every composite is possible; then the necessary in itself would be possible in itself." We say: We do not accept that from the supposition of each being necessary in itself composition necessarily follows. Its explanation is from [several] aspects; one of them: If we assume that the necessity of existence (wujub al-wujud) is a negative attribute, then each of them shares with the other in a negative attribute, and each is distinct from the other in the entirety of the essence. Sharing a negative attribute does not entail composition in the essence; the proof is that every two simple essences must share in the negation of what is other than them from them. If sharing in negations entailed multiplicity in the essence, then every simple would be composite, which is impossible. Thus we know that assuming necessity of existence is an attribute does not entail multiplicity.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and the author's initial reply. The objector argues that if there were two necessary beings, they would share the attribute of essential necessity and differ in their specific identity; this would make each composite (since they have a common attribute and a distinguishing factor), and composition implies possibility, contradicting necessity. The author denies that composition follows, and gives one reason: if necessity of existence (wujub) is a negative attribute (sifah sallabiyyah), then sharing a negative attribute does not produce composition. He illustrates: two simple essences share the negation of what is other than them, yet this does not make them composite. Thus, the assumption that wujub is negative prevents the argument from going through.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sharing any attribute with another being makes that being composite.
Correction: Razi shows that sharing a negative attribute does not entail composition, as simple essences share negations without becoming composite.

Checkpoint
According to the reply, why does sharing a negative attribute not imply composition?
A) Because negative attributes are not real properties
B) Because two simples always share negations without becoming composite
C) Because composition requires positive attributes
D) Because necessity is a positive attribute

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the composition objection by arguing that sharing a negative attribute does not imply composition, using the example of two simple essences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's oneness, do you ever unconsciously assume that God is 'composed' of attributes? How does realizing that some attributes are merely negative change your mental picture of Him?
?
Razi uses a logical argument about simple essences. Are you willing to study such reasoning deeply to purify your understanding of tawhid, even if it feels abstract?
?
If sharing a negative attribute does not cause composition, what does that imply for your own relationships? Do you mistakenly think that sharing a common negative (e.g., both avoiding a sin) makes you 'connected' in a way that distracts from true union on good?

First Proof of Wujub as Negative: Avoiding Regress
First proof: if wujub is positive, it leads to regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wujub cannot be a positive attribute without leading to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
If wujub were positive, the Necessary would be contingent or cause endless regress.

Imam Razi begins his response by tackling the very definition of wujub. He argues that if wujub were a positive attribute, it would force the Necessary of Existence into absurd consequences. The first proof uses the impossibility of infinite regress to show that wujub must be negative.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation for the first proof. Notice how Razi sets up the conditional: if wujub is positive, then two possibilities.
2
Follow the regress argument
Trace the logic: if the quiddity's existence is not necessary, then wujub is contingent; if necessary, then that necessity is a further attribute, leading to regress.
Razi uses the principle that what is shared (existence) is different from what differentiates (quiddity).
3
See the conclusion
Understand that the regress is impossible, so the premise that wujub is positive must be false.
This proof relies on the well-known kalam principle that infinite regress is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الأول) فما الدليل على أن الوجوب ليس وصفًا سلبيًا ثم الذي يدل على أن الوجوب وصف سلبي وجوه :
أحدها : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان مساويًا لسائر الموجودات في الوجود، ومخالفًا لها في ماهيتها المخصوصة وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة. فالوجود بالذات لو كان أمرًا ثبوتيًا لكانت ماهيته مغايرة لوجوده، فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إما أن يكون واجبًا وإما أن لا يكون، فإن لم يكن واجبًا كان الوجوب الذاتي ممكن الوجود لذاته، فكان الواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته، وذلك محال، وإن كان واجبًا فهذا الوجوب صفة لاتصاف تلك الماهية بذلك الوجود، فيكون وجوب ذلك الوجود مغايرا له، ويكون الكلام فيه كما في الأول، فيلزم التسلسل، وهو محال.
وثانيهما : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان إما أن يكون عبارة عن تمام تلك الحقيقة المحكوم عليها بالوجوب، وإما أن يكون جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة، وإما أن يكون أمرًا خارجًا عن تلك الحقيقة، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فالقول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطل. وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع أن يكون الوجوب تمام تلك الحقيقة والماهية وذلك لأن تلك الماهية محكوم عليها بأنها واجبة، والموضوع يمتنع أن يكون عين المحمول؛ لأن ماهية واجب الوجود غير معلومة والمعلوم ليس هو نفس ما هو غير معلوم. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة لأن على هذا التقدير تكون تلك الحقيقة مركبة، وقد بيَّنتم أن كل مركب ممكن فإنه يلزم أن يكون الواجب لذاته ممكنا لذاته، وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة لأن كل ما كان صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة مفتقر إليها كان تحققه متوقفًا على تحقق تلك الحقيقة، وكل ما كان كذلك كان ممكنا لذاته، فذلك الوجوب بالذات ممكن لذاته، وإذا كان الوجوب ممكنا بالذات كان الواجب بالذات أولى بأن يكون ممكنا بالذات فثبت أن الأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فكان القول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطلا.
وثالثها: أن الوجوب محمول على العدم والمحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا، فالوجوب يمتنع أن يكون ثابتاً، وإنما قلنا إن الوجوب محمول على العدم لأن كل ما يصدق عليه أنه يمتنع أن يوجد يصدق عليه أنه يجب أن لا يوجد، فالوجوب محمول على لا وجود فثبت أن مفهوم الوجوب محمول على العدم، وإنما قلنا إن المحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا لأنه ثبت في بدائه العقول أن قيام الصفة الموجودة بالنفي المحض محال. فثبت بهذه البراهين الثلاثة أن الوجوب صفة عدمية، وثبت أن الاشتراك في الصفة العدمية لا يوجب وقوع الكثرة في الماهية، فثبت أنه لا يلزم من اشتراك الشيئين في الوجوب وقوع الاشتراك في ماهيتهما.
The first objection: What is the proof that wujub is not a negative attribute? Then that which indicates that wujub is a negative attribute are aspects: First: That if wujub (necessity) were a positive attribute, it would be equal to other existents in existence and different from them in their specific quiddity, and that by which there is sharing is other than that by which there is distinction. So existence-in-itself (al-wujud bi al-dhat) if it were a positive thing, its quiddity would be other than its existence. Then the attribution of its quiddity to its existence is either necessary or not. If it is not necessary, then essential necessity (al-wujub al-dhati) would be possible in itself, so the Necessary in Itself would be more deserving of being possible in itself, and that is impossible. And if it is necessary, then this necessity is an attribute of the quiddity's being characterized by that existence, so the necessity of that existence is other than it, and the discussion about it is as in the first, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. Second: That if wujub were a positive attribute, it would either be the entirety of that essence (haqiqah) which is judged to be necessary, or a part of that essence, or something external to that essence. All three divisions are false, so the statement that wujub is a positive thing is false. And we said that it is impossible for wujub to be the entirety of that essence and quiddity because that quiddity is judged to be necessary, and the subject cannot be identical to the predicate, because the quiddity of the Necessary of Existence (Wajib al-Wujud) is unknown, and the known is not the same as what is unknown. And we said that it is impossible for wujub to be a part of that essence because on this assumption that essence would be composite, and you have explained that every composite is possible, so it would necessitate that the Necessary in Itself be possible in itself. And we said that it is impossible for wujub to be an attribute external to the essence because everything that is an attribute external to the essence and dependent on it has its realization dependent on the realization of that essence, and everything that is like that is possible in itself. So that necessity-in-itself is possible in itself, and if wujub is possible in itself, then the Necessary in Itself is more deserving of being possible in itself. So it is established that the three divisions are false, and thus the statement that wujub is a positive thing is false. Third: That wujub is predicated of non-existence (al-'adam), and that which is predicated of non-existence cannot be established, so wujub cannot be established. And we said that wujub is predicated of non-existence because everything of which it is true that it is impossible for it to exist, it is true of it that it must not exist. So wujub is predicated of non-existence. So it is established that the concept of wujub is predicated of non-existence. And we said that that which is predicated of non-existence cannot be established because it is established in the primary intuitions of intellects (bada'i' al-'uqul) that the subsistence of an existent attribute in pure negation is impossible. So it is established by these three proofs that wujub is a negative attribute (sifah 'adamiyyah), and it is established that sharing in a negative attribute does not necessitate the occurrence of multiplicity in the quiddity, so it is established that from the sharing of two things in wujub, the occurrence of sharing in their quiddities does not follow.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection and its answer. The objection asks for a proof that wujub (necessity) is not a negative attribute, but the answer actually provides three proofs that it is negative. The author first states that the indication that wujub is negative consists of several aspects. The first proof argues that if wujub were positive, the Necessary in Itself would be subject to composition or infinite regress. The reasoning is that if existence-in-itself were a positive attribute, its quiddity would be distinct from its existence, leading to either contingency or a regress of further necessity. The second proof divides the possibilities of wujub being positive: it could be the entire essence, a part, or external. Each is refuted: it cannot be the entire essence because the subject and predicate cannot be identical; it cannot be a part because that would make the essence composite, thus contingent; it cannot be external because then it would depend on the essence and be contingent itself. The third proof argues that wujub is predicated of non-existence (e.g., 'it must not exist'), and a positive attribute cannot be predicated of pure negation. The conclusion is that wujub is a negative attribute, and sharing in such an attribute does not entail sharing in quiddity, thus preserving God's oneness.

صفة ثبوتية
ماهية
وجود
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if wujub is negative, then God's existence is somehow deficient or not real.
Correction: Razi shows that wujub being negative actually protects God's oneness and simplicity, avoiding multiplicity in His essence.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what happens if the quiddity's existence is necessary?
A) It leads to a contradiction with divine unity.
B) It leads to an infinite regress of necessities.
C) It leads to the quiddity being composite.
D) It leads to the necessity being predicated of non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Wujub cannot be a positive attribute because that leads to either contingency or infinite regress, both of which are impossible for the Necessary of Existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider God's necessity, do you unconsciously treat it as another quality like your own attributes? How does Razi's proof challenge that tendency, and what must change in your conception of God's transcendence?
?
The proof shows that God's necessity cannot be a positive property. In your daily life, do you still think of God as having a nature that shares features with created things? What specific step can you take today to remind yourself that God's existence is utterly unlike any other?
?
If wujub were positive, it would lead to an infinite regress. Are there areas in your life where you rely on infinite reasoning to avoid facing the Absolute? How can this proof push you to stop making excuses and submit to God's unique and simple existence?

Second Proof: Division into Whole, Part, or External
Second proof: division into whole, part, or external, each refuted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wujub cannot be a positive attribute by analyzing the three possible relationships to the essence.

Core Idea
If wujub were positive, it would be the whole, part, or external to the essence — all impossible.

Razi's second proof is a powerful trichotomy: if wujub were a positive attribute, it must either be identical to the essence, a part of it, or separate from it. Through careful analysis, each option is shown to be impossible, thereby reinforcing that wujub is a negative attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof passage
Read the Arabic text and translation for the second proof. Note the logical division into three possibilities.
2
Examine why it can't be the whole
If wujub were the entire essence, then the essence would be identical to its own necessity, but the subject (essence) cannot be identical to the predicate (necessity) because the essence of Wajib al-Wujud is unknown.
This argument relies on the unknowability of God's essence.
3
Examine why it can't be a part
If wujub were a part, the essence would be composite, and every composite is contingent, contradicting necessary existence.
Composition implies dependence of parts on the whole.
4
Examine why it can't be external
If wujub were external and dependent on the essence, then it would be contingent itself, again contradicting self-necessity.
This is similar to the first proof but using dependence.
5
Conclude the impossibility
All three possibilities are false, so the assumption that wujub is positive is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الأول) فما الدليل على أن الوجوب ليس وصفًا سلبيًا ثم الذي يدل على أن الوجوب وصف سلبي وجوه :
أحدها : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان مساويًا لسائر الموجودات في الوجود، ومخالفًا لها في ماهيتها المخصوصة وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة. فالوجود بالذات لو كان أمرًا ثبوتيًا لكانت ماهيته مغايرة لوجوده، فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إما أن يكون واجبًا وإما أن لا يكون، فإن لم يكن واجبًا كان الوجوب الذاتي ممكن الوجود لذاته، فكان الواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته، وذلك محال، وإن كان واجبًا فهذا الوجوب صفة لاتصاف تلك الماهية بذلك الوجود، فيكون وجوب ذلك الوجود مغايرا له، ويكون الكلام فيه كما في الأول، فيلزم التسلسل، وهو محال.
وثانيهما : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان إما أن يكون عبارة عن تمام تلك الحقيقة المحكوم عليها بالوجوب، وإما أن يكون جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة، وإما أن يكون أمرًا خارجًا عن تلك الحقيقة، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فالقول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطل. وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع أن يكون الوجوب تمام تلك الحقيقة والماهية وذلك لأن تلك الماهية محكوم عليها بأنها واجبة، والموضوع يمتنع أن يكون عين المحمول؛ لأن ماهية واجب الوجود غير معلومة والمعلوم ليس هو نفس ما هو غير معلوم. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة لأن على هذا التقدير تكون تلك الحقيقة مركبة، وقد بيَّنتم أن كل مركب ممكن فإنه يلزم أن يكون الواجب لذاته ممكنا لذاته، وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة لأن كل ما كان صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة مفتقر إليها كان تحققه متوقفًا على تحقق تلك الحقيقة، وكل ما كان كذلك كان ممكنا لذاته، فذلك الوجوب بالذات ممكن لذاته، وإذا كان الوجوب ممكنا بالذات كان الواجب بالذات أولى بأن يكون ممكنا بالذات فثبت أن الأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فكان القول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطلا.
وثالثها: أن الوجوب محمول على العدم والمحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا، فالوجوب يمتنع أن يكون ثابتاً، وإنما قلنا إن الوجوب محمول على العدم لأن كل ما يصدق عليه أنه يمتنع أن يوجد يصدق عليه أنه يجب أن لا يوجد، فالوجوب محمول على لا وجود فثبت أن مفهوم الوجوب محمول على العدم، وإنما قلنا إن المحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا لأنه ثبت في بدائه العقول أن قيام الصفة الموجودة بالنفي المحض محال. فثبت بهذه البراهين الثلاثة أن الوجوب صفة عدمية، وثبت أن الاشتراك في الصفة العدمية لا يوجب وقوع الكثرة في الماهية، فثبت أنه لا يلزم من اشتراك الشيئين في الوجوب وقوع الاشتراك في ماهيتهما.
The first objection: What is the proof that wujub is not a negative attribute? Then that which indicates that wujub is a negative attribute are aspects: First: That if wujub (necessity) were a positive attribute, it would be equal to other existents in existence and different from them in their specific quiddity, and that by which there is sharing is other than that by which there is distinction. So existence-in-itself (al-wujud bi al-dhat) if it were a positive thing, its quiddity would be other than its existence. Then the attribution of its quiddity to its existence is either necessary or not. If it is not necessary, then essential necessity (al-wujub al-dhati) would be possible in itself, so the Necessary in Itself would be more deserving of being possible in itself, and that is impossible. And if it is necessary, then this necessity is an attribute of the quiddity's being characterized by that existence, so the necessity of that existence is other than it, and the discussion about it is as in the first, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. Second: That if wujub were a positive attribute, it would either be the entirety of that essence (haqiqah) which is judged to be necessary, or a part of that essence, or something external to that essence. All three divisions are false, so the statement that wujub is a positive thing is false. And we said that it is impossible for wujub to be the entirety of that essence and quiddity because that quiddity is judged to be necessary, and the subject cannot be identical to the predicate, because the quiddity of the Necessary of Existence (Wajib al-Wujud) is unknown, and the known is not the same as what is unknown. And we said that it is impossible for wujub to be a part of that essence because on this assumption that essence would be composite, and you have explained that every composite is possible, so it would necessitate that the Necessary in Itself be possible in itself. And we said that it is impossible for wujub to be an attribute external to the essence because everything that is an attribute external to the essence and dependent on it has its realization dependent on the realization of that essence, and everything that is like that is possible in itself. So that necessity-in-itself is possible in itself, and if wujub is possible in itself, then the Necessary in Itself is more deserving of being possible in itself. So it is established that the three divisions are false, and thus the statement that wujub is a positive thing is false. Third: That wujub is predicated of non-existence (al-'adam), and that which is predicated of non-existence cannot be established, so wujub cannot be established. And we said that wujub is predicated of non-existence because everything of which it is true that it is impossible for it to exist, it is true of it that it must not exist. So wujub is predicated of non-existence. So it is established that the concept of wujub is predicated of non-existence. And we said that that which is predicated of non-existence cannot be established because it is established in the primary intuitions of intellects (bada'i' al-'uqul) that the subsistence of an existent attribute in pure negation is impossible. So it is established by these three proofs that wujub is a negative attribute (sifah 'adamiyyah), and it is established that sharing in a negative attribute does not necessitate the occurrence of multiplicity in the quiddity, so it is established that from the sharing of two things in wujub, the occurrence of sharing in their quiddities does not follow.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection and its answer. The objection asks for a proof that wujub (necessity) is not a negative attribute, but the answer actually provides three proofs that it is negative. The author first states that the indication that wujub is negative consists of several aspects. The first proof argues that if wujub were positive, the Necessary in Itself would be subject to composition or infinite regress. The reasoning is that if existence-in-itself were a positive attribute, its quiddity would be distinct from its existence, leading to either contingency or a regress of further necessity. The second proof divides the possibilities of wujub being positive: it could be the entire essence, a part, or external. Each is refuted: it cannot be the entire essence because the subject and predicate cannot be identical; it cannot be a part because that would make the essence composite, thus contingent; it cannot be external because then it would depend on the essence and be contingent itself. The third proof argues that wujub is predicated of non-existence (e.g., 'it must not exist'), and a positive attribute cannot be predicated of pure negation. The conclusion is that wujub is a negative attribute, and sharing in such an attribute does not entail sharing in quiddity, thus preserving God's oneness.

Key Terms
وجوب
صفة ثبوتية
ماهية
حقيقة
مركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'wujub' could be a part of God's essence, like an attribute that inheres in Him.
Correction: Razi shows that any composition, including essense-plus-attribute, implies contingency, which is incompatible with necessary existence.

Checkpoint
Why cannot wujub be a part of the essence of the Necessary?
A) Because the essence is unknown.
B) Because it would lead to infinite regress.
C) Because the essence would be composite and thus contingent.
D) Because wujub is predicated of non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Wujub cannot be a positive attribute because it cannot be identical to, a part of, or separate from the essence without leading to impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God as 'Necessary of Existence', do you imagine necessity as a quality that God 'has' added to His essence? This passage shows it is not a separate attribute. Can you worship a God whose very necessity is not a distinct trait but simply His reality? How does this reshape your understanding of tawhid?
?
The argument relies on the fact that God's essence is unknowable. Are you comfortable with the mystery of God's essence, or do you subconsciously form mental images? This lesson proves wujub cannot be identical to the essence because the essence is unknown. Would you trust God more if you stopped trying to define His essence?
?
The refutation of 'external' warns that any attribute outside the essence becomes dependent and contingent. Is there any attribute of God—mercy, power, knowledge—that you treat as if it exists independently of Him? How can you purify your heart from any hint of multiplicity in God's oneness? What would change if you saw all attributes as not additional entities but as His very reality?

Third Proof: Wujub Predicated of Non-Existence
Third proof: wujub is predicated of non-existence, hence it is negative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why wujub is a negative attribute because it is predicated of non-existence.

Core Idea
Wujub is said of things that cannot exist, so it is a negative attribute.

Razi's third proof takes a different approach: he observes that the concept of necessity (wujub) is often used in statements like 'it must not exist', where the predicate attaches to non-existence. Since a positive attribute cannot subsist in pure negation, wujub itself must be a negative attribute. This proof ties together the earlier arguments and shows that sharing in a negative attribute does not imply sharing in quiddity.

Guided Path
1
Read the third proof passage
Read the Arabic text and translation for the third proof. Notice the key move: wujub is predicated of non-existence.
The example: 'it is impossible to exist' implies 'it must not exist'.
2
Understand the predication on non-existence
Razi claims that wujub applies to things that do not exist, e.g., 'the partner of God must not exist' – here wujub is said of a non-existent.
3
Grasp why such predication is impossible for a positive attribute
A positive attribute cannot inhere in pure non-existence, because existence is a prerequisite for any positive quality.
This is based on primary intuitions of the intellect (bada'i' al-'uqul).
4
Draw the conclusion
Since wujub is predicated of non-existence, it cannot be a positive attribute; it must be negative. And sharing in a negative attribute does not imply sharing in quiddity.
This final point preserves the oneness of God: all necessary beings share 'wujub', but that does not make them equal in essence.

According to the third proof, why cannot wujub be a positive attribute?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Is there an area of your life where you have subconsciously claimed a form of necessity for yourself—like feeling 'I must have this job' or 'I cannot live without this person'? How does this truth expose that as a false claim to divine immutability?
?
The proof rests on the principle that a positive attribute cannot subsist in pure non-existence. Have you ever considered that your own existence is pure contingency—it could have been non-existence. Does that thought humble you enough to drop any pretense of self-importance? What will you do today to remember that only God has real necessity?

Three Proofs That Ta'ayyun Is Not a Positive Attribute
Razi presents three proofs that ta'ayyun is not a positive attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that ta'ayyun (determination) is not a positive attribute and how three proofs (infinite regress, circularity, and infinite multiplication) demonstrate this.

Core Idea
Ta'ayyun cannot be a positive attribute without causing logical absurdities.

In the second objection, the opponent grants that wujub is positive but denies that ta'ayyun is positive. Razi not only accepts this denial but proves it with three powerful arguments. These proofs reveal that treating ta'ayyun as an additional attribute leads to impossible consequences like infinite regress, circularity, and the infinite multiplication of essences. This lesson examines each proof to understand why ta'ayyun must be non-positive.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection and Razi's stance
Read the passage's opening lines that present the objection and Razi's claim that ta'ayyun is not positive. Notice how Razi immediately counters the opponent's position.
The opponent concedes wujub is positive but denies ta'ayyun is positive; Razi agrees and provides proofs.
2
Examine the first proof: infinite regress
Read the first proof carefully. It argues that if ta'ayyun were additional, each determination would need another determination to distinguish it, leading to an infinite regress. Follow the logical steps.
Look for the argument that individuals of determinations are equal in quiddity but distinct by their own ta'ayyun.
3
Examine the second and third proofs
Read the second proof (circularity) and third proof (infinite multiplication). Note how each proof starts from the assumption that ta'ayyun is additional and derives an impossibility.
The third proof shows that even a single thing would become infinite in number if ta'ayyun were additional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثاني : سلمنا أن الوجوب صفة ثبوتية لكن لا نسلم أن التعين أمر ثبوتي، بل نقول : التعين ليس بأمر ثبوتي وإذا كان كذلك لا يلزم من حصول المباينة في التعين وقوع التركيب في الماهية.
والذي يدل على أن التعين ليس أمرا ثبوتيًا وجوه
أحدها: أن تعين كل شيء متعين غير تعين المتعين الآخر، وإلا لكان تعين كل شيء عين تعين غيره وعلى هذا التقدير يلزم أن تكون الأشياء كلها متعينة بتعين واحد، وهو محال، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : أفراد التعينات متساوية في ماهية كونها تعينا، وكل واحد من تلك الأفراد يباين الآخر بتعينه فيلزم أن يكون تعين المتعين زائدا عليه، ثم الكلام في الثاني كما في الأول فيلزم التسلسل وهو محال.
وثانيها : وهو أن التعين لو كان زائدا على الذات لكان اختصاص ذلك الزائد المسمى بالتعين بهذه الذات دون تلك الذات يتوقف على امتياز هذه الذات عن تلك الذات ولكن امتياز هذه الذات عن تلك الذات يتوقف على تعين هذه الذات وتلك الذات، فلو كان تعين هذه الذات وتعين تلك الذات معللا بذلك الزائد وقع الدور، وإنه محال.
وثالثها : لو كان التعين وصفًا زائدا على الذات لكان المتعين لم يكن في نفسه شيئًا واحداً، بل كان شيئين : أحدهما : تلك الذات والثاني : الصفة والمسماة بالتعين القائمة بالذات، وإذا كانا شيئين ولكل واحد منهما تعين فلا يكون ذلك الشيء اثنين بل أربعة، ثم لكل واحد من تلك الأربعة تعين آخر، فلا يكون ذلك أربعة بل ثمانية، وهلم جرا، فيلزم من ذلك أن الشيء الذي حكمنا عليه بأنه واحد ليس بواحد بل أعداد غير متناهية، وذلك محال؛ لأن الواحد لا يكون عدداً، وأيضًا فإن الكثرة عبارة عن مجموع الوحدات فلا بد هناك من وحدة، لكن تلك الوحدة لها تعين فلا تكون الوحدة وحدة، هذا خلف.
The second objection: We grant that wujub is a positive attribute, but we do not grant that ta'ayyun (determination) is a positive thing. Rather, we say: ta'ayyun is not a positive thing, and if so, the occurrence of distinction in ta'ayyun does not necessitate the occurrence of composition in the quiddity. And that which indicates that ta'ayyun is not a positive thing are aspects: One: That the ta'ayyun of each determinate thing is other than the ta'ayyun of another determinate thing; otherwise the ta'ayyun of everything would be identical to the ta'ayyun of another, and on this assumption it would necessitate that all things be determined by one ta'ayyun, which is impossible. And if this is established, we say: The individuals of determinations (afrad al-ta'ayyunat) are equal in the quiddity of being a determination, and each one of those individuals is distinct from another by its ta'ayyun, so it would necessitate that the ta'ayyun of the determinate be additional to it, then the discussion about the second is as in the first, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. Two: That if ta'ayyun were additional to the essence, then the specification of that additional thing called ta'ayyun to this essence rather than that essence would depend on the distinction of this essence from that essence, but the distinction of this essence from that essence depends on the ta'ayyun of this essence and that essence. So if the ta'ayyun of this essence and the ta'ayyun of that essence are caused by that additional thing, a circularity (dawr) would occur, and it is impossible. Three: If ta'ayyun were an attribute additional to the essence, then the determinate thing would not be in itself one thing, but two things: one is that essence, and the second is the attribute called ta'ayyun subsisting in the essence. And if they are two things, and each of them has a ta'ayyun, then that thing would not be two but four; then for each of those four there is another ta'ayyun, so it would not be four but eight, and so on. So it would necessitate that the thing which we judged to be one is not one but infinite numbers, and that is impossible, because the one is not a number. Also, multiplicity is the sum of unities, so there must be a unity, but that unity has a ta'ayyun, so the unity would not be a unity; this is a contradiction.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection and its answer. The opponent concedes that wujub might be positive but argues that ta'ayyun (determination) is not positive, so distinction in ta'ayyun does not imply composition in the quiddity. The author then provides three proofs that ta'ayyun is indeed not a positive attribute. The first proof shows that if ta'ayyun were positive and additional, each determination would need another determination to distinguish it from others, leading to infinite regress. The second proof argues that if ta'ayyun were an additional attribute, it would cause circularity: the specification of the additional attribute to a particular essence depends on the essence's distinction, which in turn depends on ta'ayyun. The third proof shows that if ta'ayyun were additional, the determinate thing would split into essence and attribute, each requiring its own determination, leading to an infinite multiplication and contradicting its unity. The conclusion is that ta'ayyun is not positive, so distinction in ta'ayyun does not entail composition.

Key Terms
تعين
صفة ثبوتية
ذات
تسلسل
دور
وحدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that ta'ayyun (determination) is a positive attribute that can be added to the divine essence without problem.
Correction: Razi shows that treating ta'ayyun as a positive attribute leads to logical absurdities: infinite regress, circularity, and infinite multiplication. Therefore, ta'ayyun must be non-positive.

Checkpoint
What is the second proof's argument against ta'ayyun being additional to the essence?
A) It leads to infinite regress.
B) It leads to circularity because the specification of ta'ayyun depends on essence distinction and vice versa.
C) It leads to an infinite number of determinations for a single thing.
D) It contradicts the definition of ta'ayyun.

Key Takeaway
Ta'ayyun is not a positive attribute; treating it as such leads to logical contradictions (infinite regress, circularity, infinite multiplication), thus preserving the simplicity of the divine essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on Allah's oneness (tawheed), do you ever unconsciously imagine His 'distinctiveness' as a quality added to His essence, like the distinctiveness of created things? How does this lesson's first proof—that such a view leads to infinite regress—challenge that assumption in your own mind? What practical step can you take today to remind yourself that Allah's oneness is absolutely simple?
?
Razi's second proof shows a circular dependency if taʿayyun were positive: the attribute needs the essence to be distinguished, but the essence needs the attribute to be distinguished. Have you ever felt a similar circularity in your own understanding of Allah—perhaps trying to define Him using categories that only apply to creation? What does this teach you about the limits of human reason in approaching Allah?
?
The third proof demonstrates that if taʿayyun were additional, the 'one' would become an infinite number of things. When you contemplate the verse 'Say: He is Allah, the One' (Quran 112:1), do you really mean it, or do you subtly imagine a composite being? How will this proof change the way you internalize the meaning of 'al-Aḥad' in your daily worship?

Proof from Essential Entailments
First proof: essential entailments imply many necessary beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how essential entailments (such as oddness following from three) imply multiple necessary beings, challenging the claim of oneness.

Core Idea
Essential entailments are necessary in themselves, so there are many necessary things.

Imam Razi presents the first of three arguments showing that multiplicity of necessary beings is unavoidable regardless of whether one accepts a single Necessary Being. This argument focuses on the phenomenon of essential entailments—relationships like 'three entails oddness'—which themselves seem to be necessary and many, implying multiple necessities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice how the argument progresses from examples to a general conclusion.
The examples are specific (three, four, blackness) to illustrate the concept.
2
Identify the key claim
The argument claims that essential entailments (e.g., three entails oddness) are necessities in themselves. Since there are many such entailments, there are many necessary beings.
This directly challenges the idea that only one being is necessary.
3
Ask: why does this matter?
Reflect on the broader implication: if even abstract relationships are necessary, then oneness of the Necessary Being is contradicted.
This is one of several arguments that attempt to show multiplicity is inevitable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثالث : سلمنا أنه يلزم من حصول الاشتراك في الوجوب وحصول التباين في التعين وقوع الكثرة في الماهية لكن هذه الكثرة لازمة، سواء قلنا بأن واجب الوجود واحدًا أو لم نقل به، وبيانه من وجوه : أحدها: أنه لا شك أن هنا لوازم وملزومات فإن الثلاثة مستلزمة لذاتها لمعنى الفردية والأربعة مستلزمة لمعنى الزوجية والسواد لذاته مناف للبياض، فهذه الاستلزامات الذاتية وجوبات ذاتية وهي أنواع كثيرة فإن واجب الوجود لذاته أكثر من واحد. وثانيها : هب أن واجب الوجود لذاته ليس إلا واحداً، لكن الواجب بغيره فيه كثرة، ثم الواجب لذاته يشارك الواجب بغيره في مسمى كونه واجباً، ويمتاز عنه بخصوص كونه واجبًا لذاته وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة، فالواجب بالذات مركب في ماهيته وحينئذ تعود المحالات المذكورة. وثالثها: أن واجب الوجود لذاته يساوي في كونه موجودا سائر الموجودات ويباينها بتعينه وذلك التعين إما أن يكون سلبيًا أو ثبوتياً، فإن كان ذلك التعين سلبيًا يكون هو من حيث إنه هو عدما لا وجوداً، وذلك محال، فإذن ذلك التعين الذي به باين غيره أمر ثبوتي، فإذن هو مركب عن الوجود الذي به يشارك غيره، وعن التعين الذي به امتاز عن غيره، فيلزم وقوع الكثرة في ذاته.
The third question: We grant that from participation in necessity and difference in determination, multiplicity in essence follows, but this multiplicity is necessary whether we say the Necessary Being is one or not. Explanation: First, there is no doubt that there are entailers and entailments: three entails oddness, four entails evenness, blackness is opposed to whiteness. These essential entailments are necessities in themselves and are of many types. So the Necessary Being in itself is more than one. Second, suppose that the Necessary Being in itself is only one, but the necessary by another has multiplicity. Then the necessary in itself shares with the necessary by another in the meaning of being necessary, and is distinguished by its specificity of being necessary in itself. That by which participation occurs is different from that by which distinction occurs. So the necessary by essence is composite in its essence, and then the aforementioned impossibilities return. Third, the necessary in itself equals all existents in being existent and differs from them by its determination. That determination is either negative or positive. If it is negative, then it is, in that aspect, non-existence, not existence—impossible. So that determination by which it differs from others is a positive matter. Therefore it is composed of existence, by which it shares with others, and of determination, by which it is distinguished from others. Hence multiplicity in its essence follows.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is the third objection attacking the argument for oneness by showing that multiplicity of necessary beings is unavoidable in any case. The objector presents three arguments: 1) Essential entailments (e.g., three entails oddness) are themselves necessary in some sense, so there are multiple necessary things. 2) Even if only one necessary-by-itself exists, there are necessary-by-others (contingent things that become necessary when their cause exists). The necessary-by-itself shares necessity with them but is distinguished by being self-necessary, so it is composite. 3) If the necessary-by-itself shares existence with all existents and is distinguished by a positive determination, it is composite of existence and determination, leading to multiplicity in its essence.

Key Terms
اللوازم والملزومات
الوجوب الذاتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what does the entailment 'three entails oddness' demonstrate?
A) That oddness is contingent
B) That there is a necessary relationship which itself is a necessity
C) That three is not a number
D) That all entailments are identical

Key Takeaway
Essential entailments are many necessary relationships, implying that multiple necessary beings exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the necessary order in the universe—like cause and effect, or the mathematical truths that never fail—do you recognize them as signs of the One Necessary Being, or do you take them for granted? What would change if you saw every 'essential entailment' as a reminder of Allah's necessity?
?
This passage argues that necessity itself is multiple. Yet your heart often clings to created things as if they were necessary for your happiness. Which 'false necessities' are you holding onto right now—career, relationships, comfort—that compete with the true necessity of Allah? How can you begin to release them today?
?
The proof points to many necessary relationships existing independently. If everything necessary points back to Allah, then your existence as a contingent being demands that you align your will entirely with the Necessary. Are there areas of your life where you are trying to be self-sufficient? Will you admit your complete need for Him and let go of that illusion?
