Proof from Necessary-by-Other and Composition
Second proof: necessary by itself and necessary by other lead to composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the distinction between 'necessary by itself' and 'necessary by another' leads to composition in the essence of the Necessary Being, implying multiplicity.

Core Idea
Even if only one being is necessary by itself, necessary-by-others exist, and their shared necessity with it forces composition.

The second argument from Razi's third objection assumes for the sake of argument that there is only one necessary-by-itself. It then introduces the category of 'necessary by another'—things that become necessary when their cause exists. The argument shows that the necessary-by-itself shares the attribute of necessity with these others, but is distinguished by being necessary in itself. This leads to composition in its essence, which was earlier argued to be impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the hypothetical assumption and the reasoning that follows.
The phrase 'هب أن' indicates a supposition.
2
Trace the argument's logical steps
Identify the claim: the necessary-by-itself shares 'being necessary' with necessary-by-others, but differs by being necessary in itself. The basis of sharing and distinguishing must be different, hence composition.
This mirrors the classic argument that if two things share a property and differ by another, they are composite.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that if the necessary-by-itself is composite, then it cannot be unitary, and the impossibility of composition (as argued earlier) would apply.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثالث : سلمنا أنه يلزم من حصول الاشتراك في الوجوب وحصول التباين في التعين وقوع الكثرة في الماهية لكن هذه الكثرة لازمة، سواء قلنا بأن واجب الوجود واحدًا أو لم نقل به، وبيانه من وجوه : أحدها: أنه لا شك أن هنا لوازم وملزومات فإن الثلاثة مستلزمة لذاتها لمعنى الفردية والأربعة مستلزمة لمعنى الزوجية والسواد لذاته مناف للبياض، فهذه الاستلزامات الذاتية وجوبات ذاتية وهي أنواع كثيرة فإن واجب الوجود لذاته أكثر من واحد. وثانيها : هب أن واجب الوجود لذاته ليس إلا واحداً، لكن الواجب بغيره فيه كثرة، ثم الواجب لذاته يشارك الواجب بغيره في مسمى كونه واجباً، ويمتاز عنه بخصوص كونه واجبًا لذاته وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة، فالواجب بالذات مركب في ماهيته وحينئذ تعود المحالات المذكورة. وثالثها: أن واجب الوجود لذاته يساوي في كونه موجودا سائر الموجودات ويباينها بتعينه وذلك التعين إما أن يكون سلبيًا أو ثبوتياً، فإن كان ذلك التعين سلبيًا يكون هو من حيث إنه هو عدما لا وجوداً، وذلك محال، فإذن ذلك التعين الذي به باين غيره أمر ثبوتي، فإذن هو مركب عن الوجود الذي به يشارك غيره، وعن التعين الذي به امتاز عن غيره، فيلزم وقوع الكثرة في ذاته.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that even the Necessary Being cannot share a universal concept without forcing composition. Now look at your own life: How many aspects of your identity—your status, knowledge, existence—are actually borrowed from others? Can you point to one thing that is truly yours by yourself? If nothing, what does that mean for your self-reliance before Allah today? Will you let go of one false sense of independence today and openly acknowledge your complete dependence on Him?
?
The proof shows that the Necessary Being is unique and incomposite. Contrast that with your own heart, which is divided by multiple attachments and loyalties. How many 'necessities' do you serve besides Allah? What concrete step will you take after this lesson to simplify your devotion to the One who alone is necessary by Himself?
?
The passage uses the concepts of sharing and distinction to argue for composition. Reflect on your prayer: when you recite 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in', you affirm that worship and aid come only from Allah. Does your heart truly make that distinction, or do you share your reliance among other things? What specific action will you change today to ensure your worship is purely for Him?

Proof from Determination (Ta'ayyun)
Third proof: determination as positive attribute forces composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the necessary being's determination (متعين) must be a positive attribute, leading to composition of existence and determination.

Core Idea
If determination is negative, the being would be non-existence; so it's positive, causing composition.

The third proof focuses on the concept of determination (تعين) that distinguishes the Necessary Being from other existents. The argument explores whether this determination is negative (i.e., just the absence of other attributes) or positive (a real attribute). If negative, then the being would in that aspect be mere non-existence, which is absurd. Therefore, determination must be positive, leading to composition of existence and determination, and thus multiplicity in essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the text carefully, especially the dichotomy between negative and positive determination.
The argument is a classic dilemma: either the distinction is negative or positive.
2
Work through the dichotomy
Understand why negative determination is impossible: if the Necessary Being is distinct only by a negation, then in that respect it would be non-existence.
This assumes that a real distinction cannot be based on pure negation.
3
Conclude the argument
Since determination must be positive, the Necessary Being is composed of existence (shared with others) and determination (unique), thus multiplicity in essence follows.
This is another angle to show composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثالث : سلمنا أنه يلزم من حصول الاشتراك في الوجوب وحصول التباين في التعين وقوع الكثرة في الماهية لكن هذه الكثرة لازمة، سواء قلنا بأن واجب الوجود واحدًا أو لم نقل به، وبيانه من وجوه : أحدها: أنه لا شك أن هنا لوازم وملزومات فإن الثلاثة مستلزمة لذاتها لمعنى الفردية والأربعة مستلزمة لمعنى الزوجية والسواد لذاته مناف للبياض، فهذه الاستلزامات الذاتية وجوبات ذاتية وهي أنواع كثيرة فإن واجب الوجود لذاته أكثر من واحد. وثانيها : هب أن واجب الوجود لذاته ليس إلا واحداً، لكن الواجب بغيره فيه كثرة، ثم الواجب لذاته يشارك الواجب بغيره في مسمى كونه واجباً، ويمتاز عنه بخصوص كونه واجبًا لذاته وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة، فالواجب بالذات مركب في ماهيته وحينئذ تعود المحالات المذكورة. وثالثها: أن واجب الوجود لذاته يساوي في كونه موجودا سائر الموجودات ويباينها بتعينه وذلك التعين إما أن يكون سلبيًا أو ثبوتياً، فإن كان ذلك التعين سلبيًا يكون هو من حيث إنه هو عدما لا وجوداً، وذلك محال، فإذن ذلك التعين الذي به باين غيره أمر ثبوتي، فإذن هو مركب عن الوجود الذي به يشارك غيره، وعن التعين الذي به امتاز عن غيره، فيلزم وقوع الكثرة في ذاته.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Fourth Objection: Composition and Contingency
Fourth objection and beginning of response about composition and contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth objection against proofs of God's unity, which argues that composition of necessary parts is possible, and the beginning of the response that every possible being requires an effecting cause.

Core Idea
Can the Necessary Being be composed of multiple necessary parts?

This lesson presents the fourth objection raised against arguments for God's unity. The objector concedes that multiplicity might follow from previous proofs but argues that each part could be necessary by itself, making the whole necessary without contradiction. The objection then shifts to challenge the claim that every possible being must be originated. We see the start of the response: the first premise that everything possible needs an effecting cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the full Arabic passage once. Notice the two parts of the objection: first about composition, then about contingency and origination.
The response is incomplete; the text cuts off mid-sentence.
2
Understand the composition argument
The objector says that even if multiplicity follows from previous arguments, each part of the essence could be necessary by itself, making the whole necessary without any problem.
3
Analyze the contingency challenge
The objector then concedes that everything other than the One is possible, but questions why every possible being must be originated (hadith).
4
Identify the response's first premise
The response begins by stating the first premise: everything possible by itself is in need of an effecting cause. The text cuts off before completing the argument.
Consider what the next premise or conclusion might be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الرابع: هب أنه يلزم من ذلك وقوع الكثرة في ذات كل واحد منهما، لكن لم لا يجوز أن يقال كل واحد من جزئي ذاته واجب لذاته، وذلك المجموع يجب لوجوب جزأيه معا وعلى هذا التقدير لا يلزم منه محذور أصلا ؟ سلمنا أن كل سوى الواحد ممكن لذاته، فلم قلتم : إن كل ممكن لذاته محدث ؟ قوله : لأن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فإنه محتاج إلى المؤثر، وكل محتاج إلى المؤثر فهو محدث قلنا : أما المقدمة الأولى وهي أن كل ما كان ممكنا لذاته فإنه
The fourth question: Grant that multiplicity in the essence of each of them follows, but why is it not permissible to say that each of the two parts of his essence is necessary by itself, and the whole is necessary due to the necessity of both parts together, and on this assumption no problem arises? We grant that everything other than the One is possible by itself, so why do you say that everything possible by itself is originated? He said: Because everything that is possible by itself is in need of an effecting cause, and everything in need of an effecting cause is originated. We say: As for the first premise, that everything that is possible by itself is...
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is the fourth objection and the beginning of the response. The objector concedes that multiplicity in the essence follows from the previous arguments, but argues that each part of the essence could be necessary by itself, so the whole is necessary without problem. Then the objector shifts to a new point: granted that everything other than the One is possible, why say that every possible being is originated (hadith)? The response begins by stating the first premise: everything possible needs an effecting cause, and everything needing a cause is originated. The text cuts off as it begins to discuss that premise.

Third Objection: Multiplicity is Necessary
Opponent argues that multiplicity in essence is necessary and unavoidable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponent argues that multiplicity in the divine essence is necessary and unavoidable, and you will analyze the three proofs presented.

Core Idea
Multiplicity in essence is inevitable, even if there is only one Necessary Existent.

This passage presents the third objection against divine unity. The opponent concedes that if two necessary beings share necessity but differ in determination, multiplicity would follow. However, he boldly claims that such multiplicity is necessary regardless of whether one affirms one or more necessary beings. He then provides three distinct proofs to support this claim. Let's explore his arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic and English
Read the complete passage once to get the flow of the objection. Notice the concessive tone ('سلمنا') and the three numbered arguments.
2
Identify the main claim
The opponent states that multiplicity is necessary whether we affirm one necessary being or not. Underline this sentence in the translation.
This is the core idea.
3
Examine the three proofs
Go through each of the three proofs: (1) essential necessities, (2) sharing and differencing, (3) determination as positive. Notice how each leads to multiplicity.
The proofs are numbered in the text.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this objection challenges the theologian's position. What would be the consequences if this argument stands?
This connects to the broader debate on tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثالث: سلمنا أنه يلزم من حصول الاشتراك في الوجوب وحصول التباين في التعين وقوع الكثرة في الماهية لكن هذه الكثرة لازمة، سواء قلنا بأن واجب الوجود واحدًا أو لم نقل به، وبيانه من وجوه : أحدها: أنه لا شك أن هنا لوازم وملزومات فإن الثلاثة مستلزمة لذاتها لمعنى الفردية والأربعة مستلزمة لمعنى الزوجية والسواد لذاته مناف للبياض، فهذه الاستلزامات الذاتية وجوبات ذاتية وهي أنواع كثيرة فإن واجب الوجود لذاته أكثر من واحد. وثانيها : هب أن واجب الوجود لذاته ليس إلا واحداً، لكن الواجب بغيره فيه كثرة، ثم الواجب لذاته يشارك الواجب بغيره في مسمى كونه واجباً، ويمتاز عنه بخصوص كونه واجبًا لذاته وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة، فالواجب بالذات مركب في ماهيته وحينئذ تعود المحالات المذكورة. وثالثها: أن واجب الوجود لذاته يساوي في كونه موجودا سائر الموجودات ويباينها بتعينه وذلك التعين إما أن يكون سلبيًا أو ثبوتياً، فإن كان ذلك التعين سلبيًا يكون هو من حيث إنه هو عدما لا وجوداً، وذلك محال، فإذن ذلك التعين الذي به باين غيره أمر ثبوتي، فإذن هو مركب عن الوجود الذي به يشارك غيره، وعن التعين الذي به امتاز عن غيره، فيلزم وقوع الكثرة في ذاته.
The third question: We concede that from the occurrence of sharing in necessity (wujub) and the occurrence of differentiation in determination (ta'ayyun) results multiplicity in the essence, but this multiplicity is necessary, whether we say that the Necessary Existent is one or not, and its explanation is from several aspects: First: There is no doubt that there are necessary concomitants and that which they necessitate. For example, three necessitates by its very essence the meaning of oddness, four necessitates the meaning of evenness, and blackness by its essence is incompatible with whiteness. These essential necessitations are essential necessities and they are many types, so the Necessary Existent by essence would be more than one. Second: Suppose that the Necessary Existent by essence is only one, but the necessary by another (al-wajib bi-ghayrihi) involves multiplicity. Then the necessary by essence shares with the necessary by another in the name of being necessary, and differs from it by the specificity of being necessary by essence. That by which it shares is different from that by which it differs, so the necessary by essence is composite in its essence, and then the aforementioned impossibilities return. Third: The Necessary Existent by essence equals other existents in being existent and differs from them by its determination. That determination is either negative or positive. If it is negative, then it would be non-being not existence, which is impossible. Thus the determination by which it differs from others is something positive, so it is composed of existence by which it shares with others and the determination by which it is distinguished from others, so multiplicity in its essence follows.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection against the claim that God is one. The opponent concedes that if two necessary beings share in necessity (wujub) and differ in determination (ta'ayyun), there would be multiplicity in the essence. However, he argues that this multiplicity is necessary and unavoidable. He gives three proofs: First, there are many essential necessities (wajubat dhatiyya) like the oddness of three and the evenness of four, which imply multiple wajibs. Second, even if only one Necessary by essence exists, the necessary by another (e.g., the contingent) involves multiplicity, and since the necessary by essence shares the name 'necessary' with the necessary by another but differs by being necessary by essence, composition follows. Third, the Necessary by essence shares existence with others but differs by determination; if that determination were negative, it would be non-existent, which is impossible, so it must be positive, leading to composition of existence and determination. Thus the objection shows that the opponent thinks multiplicity is inevitable, whether one affirms one necessary being or multiple.

Key Terms
وجوب
تعين
واجب الوجود
ماهية
استلزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent is asserting that there are multiple necessary beings.
Correction: The opponent is not asserting multiplicity; he is arguing that multiplicity is a necessary consequence whether one affirms one or many.

Checkpoint
What is the main claim of the third objection?
A) That multiplicity in the essence is impossible
B) That multiplicity is necessary whether one affirms one or many
C) That the Necessary Existent must be composite
D) That determination is negative

Key Takeaway
The third objection argues that multiplicity in the essence is necessary, using three proofs that challenge the simplicity of the Necessary Existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah, do you often imagine His attributes as separate 'parts' even while affirming His oneness? How does this lesson expose the subtle shirk of composition in your mental conception of God? What will you do to correct it?
?
The opponent argues that sharing in existence with other beings necessitates composition. Are you guilty of thinking of Allah as 'just another being' that happens to be the greatest? How does this lesson challenge you to see Him as utterly unique in essence?
?
This argument forces us to examine whether our understanding of tawhid is truly pure or unknowingly tainted. In your daily life, do you ever treat Allah as if He is composed of the same 'existence' as created things? What concrete steps can you take to worship Him as the One who is simple and incomparable?

The Fourth Objection: Composition from Necessary Parts
Opponent questions why composition of necessary parts is problematic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's objection that a composite of necessary-by-essence parts could be necessary without difficulty.

Core Idea
The opponent argues that a whole composed of independently necessary parts is still necessary.

The text presents the fourth objection to the argument that composition implies need. The opponent grants that multiplicity occurs, but questions why it is problematic. He proposes that each part could be necessary by itself, and the composite necessary by virtue of its parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic text aloud or silently, then follow the literal translation to grasp the exact wording of the objection.
Notice the phrase 'وجزء كل واحد منهما واجب لذاته' — 'each one of the two parts is necessary by itself.'
2
Identify the opponent's key claim
The opponent asserts that each part is necessary by itself (wajib li-dhatihi), so the whole composed of them is necessary. This avoids the problem of needing an external cause.
3
Consider why this might be problematic
Think about the implications: if each part is necessary by itself, then there would be multiple necessary beings. How might that conflict with divine simplicity?
This connects to upcoming lessons on the author's refutation.
4
Reflect on the subtlety
The objection shifts the burden: it challenges the assumption that composition necessarily implies need. Reflect on whether this solution is coherent.
The common misunderstanding is that the objection does not explain how multiple necessary parts can coexist without external dependency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الرابع: هب أنه يلزم من ذلك وقوع الكثرة في ذات كل واحد منهما، لكن لم لا يجوز أن يقال كل واحد من جزئي ذاته واجب لذاته، وذلك المجموع يجب لوجوب جزأيه معا وعلى هذا التقدير لا يلزم منه محذور أصلا؟
The fourth question: Suppose that from that follows multiplicity in the essence of each of them, but why may it not be said that each one of the two parts of its essence is necessary by itself, and that composite is necessary due to the necessity of its two parts together, and on this assumption no difficulty follows at all?
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth objection. The opponent grants that multiplicity would occur in the essence of each supposed necessary being. However, he questions why it should be problematic if we say that each part of the essence is itself necessary by essence (wajib li-dhatihi), and the composite whole becomes necessary by virtue of the necessity of its parts. The opponent claims that on this assumption, no logical difficulty arises. This objection attempts to avoid the problem of composition by asserting that the parts are independent necessary beings, so the whole is a sum of necessary parts rather than a composite requiring an external cause.

Key Terms
واجب لذاته
جزء
مجموع
محذور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent's solution is logically sound and resolves the composition problem without difficulty.
Correction: The objection does not explain how multiple necessary-by-essence parts can coexist without external dependency or contradiction to divine simplicity.

Checkpoint
What does the opponent propose as a solution to the composition problem?
A) That the parts are contingent
B) That each part is necessary by itself and the whole is necessary by its parts
C) That determination is negative
D) That the essence has no parts

Key Takeaway
The opponent attempts to avoid the problem of composition by asserting that the whole is necessary because its parts are each necessary by themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you ever act as though some areas of your life are 'necessary by themselves'—independent of your need for Allah—while other areas you admit need Him? What would it mean for your daily routine if you truly acknowledged that nothing in your existence is self-sufficient?
?
The opponent claims that combining necessary parts yields a necessary whole. Have you ever tried to combine enough good deeds or knowledge to make yourself 'worthy' before Allah, as if they could add up to independence from His mercy? Where does that assumption fail?
?
When you encounter objections like this one, do you engage with them honestly or dismiss them quickly? What would it look like to take a doubt seriously, study the refutation, and let it strengthen your conviction in tawhid?

Al-Razi's Responses to Objections on the Oneness of the Necessary Being
Al-Razi answers three objections about the multiplicity of necessary beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi refutes three key objections against the oneness of the Necessary Being by clarifying the meaning of 'wajib li-dhatihi' and distinguishing between essence and existence.

Core Idea
Shared attributes don't imply multiple necessary beings; true necessity is self-sufficiency.

In this passage, Al-Razi engages with three objections that challenge the Islamic doctrine of tawhid concerning the Necessary Being. Each objection attempts to show multiplicity by appealing to shared attributes like necessity or existence. Al-Razi systematically responds by refining the definition of 'necessary by itself' and distinguishing between essence and existence, though he acknowledges a lingering difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation to get an overview of the three objections and responses. Notice the pattern: 'قوله' introduces an objection, 'قلنا' introduces the response.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Examine the first objection
The first objection argues that necessary attributes (like three being odd) imply multiple necessary beings. Focus on Al-Razi's response: he distinguishes between 'necessary by itself' and accidental necessary attributes.
Note the definition of 'wajib li-dhatihi' as independent and self-initiating.
3
Analyze the second objection
The second objection points out that the Necessary Being shares necessity with contingent necessary beings. See how Al-Razi uses a 'negative qualification' (قيد سلبي) to distinguish them, preventing multiplicity.
4
Study the third objection and the unresolved issue
The third objection claims that sharing existence with possibles leads to multiplicity. Al-Razi distinguishes existence from essence but then raises a problem: if essence causes existence eternally, it implies effect without temporal origination. He leaves this for divine guidance.
This shows the depth of rational theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : "كون الثلاثة فردًا والأربعة زوجًا أمور واجبة لذواتها، فإذن واجب الوجود أكثر من واحد" قلنا مرادنا من قولنا واجب الوجود لذاته الموجود الذي يكون مستقلاً ومستبدأ بذاته وتحققه وهذه صفات تكون لاحقة للماهيات فلا تكون واجبة لذواتها.
قوله : "الواجب لذاته يشارك الواجب لغيره في مسمى الوجوب" قلنا : لكنه يمتاز عنه بقيد سلبي، وعلى هذا التقدير لا تلزم الكثرة.
قوله : "الواجب لذاته يشارك الممكن لذاته في مسمى الموجودية ويخالفه في التعين فتلزم الكثرة" قلنا : مذهبنا أن الوجود الذي به المشاركة مغاير للماهية المخصوصة التي بها المخالفة لكن لم لا يجوز أن تكون تلك الماهية مستلزمة لذلك الوجود؟ إلا أنه يبقى ههنا إشكال وهو أنكم لما جعلتم تلك الماهية علة لذلك الوجود، مع كون الماهية والوجود دائمين فقد اعترفتم بأن استناد الأثر إلى المؤثر لا يتوقف على الحدوث، وهذا الإشكال مما نستخير الله تعالى فيه.
He said: "The fact that three is odd and four is even are things necessary by themselves, so the Necessary Being is more than one." We said: What we mean by "Necessary Being by virtue of itself" is the existent that is independent and initiated by itself and its actualization. These attributes are accidents of essences, so they are not necessary by themselves.
He said: "The Necessary Being by virtue of itself shares with the necessary by virtue of another in the meaning of necessity." We said: But it is distinguished from it by a negative qualification, and on this basis multiplicity does not arise.
He said: "The Necessary Being by virtue of itself shares with the possible by virtue of itself in the meaning of existence and differs in determination, so multiplicity arises." We said: Our doctrine is that the existence by which there is participation is other than the specific essence by which there is difference. But why is it not possible that that essence necessitates that existence? Except that there remains here an objection: that you have made that essence a cause for that existence, while the essence and existence are eternal, so you have acknowledged that the dependence of the effect on the cause does not require temporal origination. This objection is one in which we seek divine guidance.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents three objections against the oneness of the Necessary Being and the author's responses. The first objection cites necessary attributes like odd and even being necessary by themselves, implying multiple necessary beings. The response clarifies that 'necessary by itself' means independent and self-initiating, not accidental attributes. The second objection points out that the Necessary Being shares necessity with contingent necessary beings. The response notes that they differ by a negative qualification, so no multiplicity follows. The third objection highlights that the Necessary Being shares existence with possibles but differs in determination. The response distinguishes existence from essence but raises an unresolved problem: if a specific essence necessitates existence eternally, then the effect depends on the cause without temporal origination, which the author leaves for divine guidance.

Key Terms
wajib al-wujud
al-wajib bi-ghayrihi
al-mumkin
al-mawjudiyya
al-qayd al-salbi
al-huduth

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If multiple things share an attribute like necessity or existence, there must be multiple necessary beings.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that the meaning of 'necessary by itself' is unique to the Necessary Being because it is independent and self-initiating. Shared attributes do not entail multiplicity when the distinction is based on causation and essence-existence relation.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi, what does 'wajib al-wujud li-dhatihi' mean?
A) Any necessary attribute
B) The existent that is independent and self-initiating
C) The one that shares existence with others
D) The composite being

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's responses show that true oneness of the Necessary Being is preserved by understanding that shared attributes do not necessitate multiplicity when meanings are properly distinguished.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to examine your own life, what 'necessary' things do you rely on that are actually dependent on others? How does this lesson challenge your sense of self-sufficiency?
?
Al-Razi honestly admits an unresolved problem and seeks divine guidance. Are you willing to leave certain profound questions unanswered, trusting in God rather than forcing a false certainty?
?
The Necessary Being is truly independent. In what areas of your life are you still trying to be self-sufficient, refusing to acknowledge your total dependence on God? What concrete step can you take today to surrender that illusion?
